  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0522809f-a4f8-4283-a0c5-91f67f13687e'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: $('box').getStyle('z-index')})});
        } else {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function(i){i.setStyle({zIndex: 6000})});
        }
      });

      newTip['wrapper'].addClassName('prototipAllowOverflow');

        $('edition_548668').observe('prototip:shown', function () {
          $$('div.prototip').each(function (e) {
            if ($('edition_548668').hasClassName('ignored')) {
              e.setStyle({'display': 'none'});
              return;
            }
            e.setStyle({'overflow': 'visible'});
          });
        });
      $('edition_548668').observe('prototip:hidden', function () {
        $$('span.elementTwo').each(function (e) {
          if (e.getStyle('display') !== 'none') {
            var lessLink = e.next();

        });

<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">You can! The storylines for Tithe and Ironside are directly connected, but Valiant is more like a 'companion piece' where theres the same kinds of cha<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">You can! The storylines for Tithe and Ironside are directly connected, but Valiant is more like a 'companion piece' where theres the same kinds of characters, and there is like one or two characters who cross over but its not anything where you would be vastly confused. It could function as a book on its own very easily<br /><a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2469917722" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2469917722" />
    <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines"><img alt="Elle (ellexamines)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582250895p2/52545435.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2469917722?book_show_action=true">Aug 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Elle (ellexamines)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Elle (ellexamines)" href="/user/show/52545435-elle-ellexamines">Elle (ellexamines)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-series">x-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-audiobook">x-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-characters">favorite-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=elle-recs-list">elle-recs-list</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=x-buylist">x-buylist</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=y-out2000">y-out2000</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=favorite-relationships">favorite-relationships</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=z-read2019">z-read2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/52545435-elle-ellexamines?shelf=sff-pn-urban-fantasy">sff-pn-urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2469917722" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17421146389598732441"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Ravus nodded again. “I will make you as terrible as you desire.”<br/>“I don't want to be-,” she started, but he held up his hand.<br/>“I know you're very brave,” he said.<br/>“Or stupid.”<br/>“And stupid. Brave and stupid.” Ravus smiled, but then his smile sagged. “But nothing can stop you from being terrible once you've learned how.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Holly Black has, apparently, been crafting marvelous worlds and characters for quite a long time now. I adored this story even more than her earlier <i>Tithe</i>. <br/><br/><i>Valiant</i> is a <b>Bea</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17421146389598732441" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>Ravus nodded again. “I will make you as terrible as you desire.”<br />“I don't want to be-,” she started, but he held up his hand.<br />“I know you're very brave,” he said.<br />“Or stupid.”<br />“And stupid. Brave and stupid.” Ravus smiled, but then his smile sagged. “But nothing can stop you from being terrible once you've learned how.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Holly Black has, apparently, been crafting marvelous worlds and characters for quite a long time now. I adored this story even more than her earlier <i>Tithe</i>. <br /><br /><i>Valiant</i> is a <b>Beauty and the Beast retelling</b> following Val, who, upon running away from home, falls in with some pals on the subway. Upon running into a troll named Ravus, she finds herself falling deeper and deeper into the faerie world – and maybe in love. Everyone is completely awful, everyone makes really big mistakes, and you cannot look away.<br /><br />Woo! Okay. So this book was just an absolutely wild ride. Holly Black’s writing is so, so engrossing – she is just <b>absolutely magical</b>. The plot is twisty and creepy; you can almost <i>feel</i> the book getting darker by the moment, as Val falls increasingly into drug addiction and into the faerie world. The characters are not exactly likable but remain compelling; <b>no one feels good and no one feels bad.</b> The romance is equally compelling, with the love interest’s backstory standing out is absolutely incredible. And the book deals well with the idea of <b>becoming haunted by a friend’s death</b>; despite the fantastical outer layer of the story, the emotional core is quite solid. <br /><br />And since Holly’s faerie world is overlapping over itself, let’s talk about <b>how well she’s crafted this universe,</b> shall we? The idea of the seelie court vs. the unseelie court is a common one, and the concept of morally grey fairies is not new. But it’s been said before and will be said again: <b>no one writes fairies like Holly Black.</b> The delicious evil, mixed with bits and pieces of humanity, is somehow equal bits enthralling and repulsive. I felt the thematic core and character writing of this book was far stronger than that of Holly Black’s debut, <i>Tithe</i>, but her fairy writing has remained excellent from the start. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“She thought of something her mother had told her when she'd finally broken up with one of her most dysfunctional boyfriends. When a man tells you he's going to hurt you, believe it. They always warn you and they're always right.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Holly Black’s love of ladies and of lady knights is consistent and honestly my favorite thing about her canon. Her female characters are so deliciously and delightfully morally gray: <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360699629?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe’s</a> Kaye, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1549797381?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Coldest Girl’s</a> Tana, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1761765969?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Darkest Part’s</a> Hazel, and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1961496305?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">The Cruel Prince’s</a> Jude are each very different, but they share a core of strength and willingness to do messed up things for their reasons. She writes characters who are consciously mean and consciously kind and focuses on their agency. Despite the terrible circumstances Val finds herself in, the romance of this story is built on firm ground from the lead’s side. <br /><br />This was <a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com/2019/01/14/some-series-i-actually-do-need-to-finish-in-2019/" rel="nofollow noopener">one of the sequels I needed to read in 2019</a>, so I’m excited that I actually succeeded in reading it! Onto Ironside. <br /><br />TW: drug addiction, and a moment of serious animal murder that made me sick to my stomach. <br /><br /><a href="https://thebookishactress.wordpress.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Goodreads</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/jespergayhey" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/thebookishactress/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="http://www.youtube.com/c/thebookishactress" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17421146389598732441" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_98285199" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/98285199" />
    <a title="Heather" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2098381-heather"><img alt="Heather" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1474068564p2/2098381.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/98285199?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Heather" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Heather" href="/user/show/2098381-heather">Heather</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780689868221" href="/book/show/601632.Valiant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2098381-heather?shelf=2010">2010</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98285199" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15229039787816744909">I hated loving this book. Having read Black's <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_' title='Tithe (The Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a>and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___3_' title='Ironside (The Modern Faerie Tales, #3) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ironside</a>, I was none to keen on reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_' title='Valiant (The Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Valiant</a>. Black has a penchant for writing about the scourge of human society, leaving me with a sense of filth, and therefore compelling me to exfoliate. None the less, Black’s writing is so perversely alluring, that she all but grabs you by the neck and drags you into the story.<br/><br/>Val is impossible to describe. She’s a shell of a girl. In possession of one lezzie best friend, a mohawk donning boyfriend, </span>
  <span id="freeText15229039787816744909" style="display:none">I hated loving this book. Having read Black's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (The Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a>and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___3_" title="Ironside (The Modern Faerie Tales, #3) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Ironside</a>, I was none to keen on reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/266607.Valiant__The_Modern_Faerie_Tales___2_" title="Valiant (The Modern Faerie Tales, #2) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Valiant</a>. Black has a penchant for writing about the scourge of human society, leaving me with a sense of filth, and therefore compelling me to exfoliate. None the less, Black’s writing is so perversely alluring, that she all but grabs you by the neck and drags you into the story.<br /><br />Val is impossible to describe. She’s a shell of a girl. In possession of one lezzie best friend, a mohawk donning boyfriend, and incredibly vain and insecure mother, Val participates in her life, but couldn’t be accused of living it. When Val walks in on her mother getting it on with her boyfriend, Val flees, going nowhere, and reveling in her lack of destination. She finds herself in New York City, homeless, but free. It is here that she encounters Lolli, a blue haired Never addict, Sketchy Dave, brother to the “sighted” Luis, and joins their trio of loner losers. Val is introduced to a world that will afford you every possible pleasure you care to take, while leaving you living in squalor and slowly choking the life from you, one Never hit at a time. Val drowns in the world of fairie, and yet finds her inner strength, as well as the love she craves. But in order to save herself, and the troll she loves, Val must learn that being free to make your own bad decisions serves no purpose other than enabling you to own your destruction. <br /><br />The characters within this story suck at life. They make piss poor role models and I hope that younger readers of this book wouldn’t think that Val’s “adventure” is the least bit realistic. Val would have wound up dead, on in the very least, assaulted. These characters run from their problems, steal, take drugs, and engage in casual sex. And yet I loved this book because these characters drop f bombs, filch, become addicts, and engage in casual sex. Life isn’t always pretty, and this book captures the essence of that filth while adding a touch of whimsy, and an acceptable happy ending.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15229039787816744909" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2606793925" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2606793925" />
    <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/65321843-a"><img alt="✨ A ✨ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1604503440p2/65321843.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2606793925?book_show_action=true">Jan 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="✨ A ✨ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="✨ A ✨ " href="/user/show/65321843-a">✨ A ✨ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

<div id="review_3181229852" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3181229852" />
    <a title="Faith M ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m"><img alt="Faith M ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587515873p2/29390149.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3181229852?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Faith M ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Faith M ✨" href="/user/show/29390149-faith-m">Faith M ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=2-stars">2-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=3rd-person">3rd-person</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=dont-believe-the-hype">dont-believe-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=spooky-scary-skeletons">spooky-scary-skeletons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=why-did-i-read-this-exactly">why-did-i-read-this-exactly</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29390149-faith-m?shelf=get-thee-behind-me-satan">get-thee-behind-me-satan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3181229852" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15347198959178203997"><blockquote>
  <i>“One fine day in the middle of the night […] two dead boys got up to fight. […] Back to back they faced each other, pulled out their swords and shot one another. The deaf cop on the beat heard the noise and came and shot the two dead boys.”</i>
</blockquote><br/>So this was a big ol’ oof but I honestly thought I’d like it when I first started. The first few chapters were fine and I didn’t mind that this didn’t follow the cast of the previous book. I found that, over all, they were way more interesting as people th</span>
  <span id="freeText15347198959178203997" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>“One fine day in the middle of the night […] two dead boys got up to fight. […] Back to back they faced each other, pulled out their swords and shot one another. The deaf cop on the beat heard the noise and came and shot the two dead boys.”</i>
</blockquote><br />So this was a big ol’ oof but I honestly thought I’d like it when I first started. The first few chapters were fine and I didn’t mind that this didn’t follow the cast of the previous book. I found that, over all, they were way more interesting as people than Tithe’s characters, but they still sucked lmao<br /><br />What on earth was up with that blatant animal abuse? It made me sick, honestly, and not in a “wow! these characters are so intense” kind of way, but rather a “this chick is a straight up sociopath and I hate her with every fiber of my being” and made me want to hit Holly Black in the face with a chair. Violence breeds violence, I guess. It felt like she was trying to be edgy and cool but without anything to really say, as usual, so it all ended up feeling like she did it for the aesthetic and brutally murdering a kitten doesn’t give me ~<i>vibes</i>~ it gives me nausea.<br /><br />If I had to pick a character that I liked, I’d say probably Dave or Luis because they felt pretty consistent but also kind of like Black took Corny and cut him in half. Lolli was the aforementioned demon-spawn, and Val was annoying. Ravus was nebulous at best. Ruth? Was she a character or a piece of soggy cardboard? The world may never know.<br /><br />The second worst thing about this was undoubtedly the plot. The love story between Val and Ravus came out of absolutely nowhere when he started spilling all of his life history to her for no reason, and I just felt like I’d accidentally skipped 5 chapters. The main plot was so jumbled and confusing but the plot twist was so obvious that I was seriously hoping that it wasn’t going to happen. So when it did, I rolled my eyes so far back that I saw my last brain cell die.<br /><br />Strangely, the only thing I truly enjoyed about this book was the knowledge that if the book I’m writing is incomprehensible trash, it might still get published and become popular.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15347198959178203997" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2202152607" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14493849595988317098">Ever since I finished <i>Tithe</i> I've wanted to finish this series.. but never seemed to try and read the second book. No idea why, maybe I'm super lazy or I just never got the book.. but I'm happy to redeem myself people. <br/><br/>It follows Val Russell, who is about 17 years old, and she have a terrible life. Her family sucked a bag of dicks and her whole life spiraled down a dark ass rabbit hole. Yeah, things were not sunny on her side of the street. The grass was not greener for her. Well, her life sort o</span>
  <span id="freeText14493849595988317098" style="display:none">Ever since I finished <i>Tithe</i> I've wanted to finish this series.. but never seemed to try and read the second book. No idea why, maybe I'm super lazy or I just never got the book.. but I'm happy to redeem myself people. <br /><br />It follows Val Russell, who is about 17 years old, and she have a terrible life. Her family sucked a bag of dicks and her whole life spiraled down a dark ass rabbit hole. Yeah, things were not sunny on her side of the street. The grass was not greener for her. Well, her life sort of gets better when she finds herself within a homeless crowd. <br /><br />From this, she meets Dave, Lolli, and Luis. Things don't always go according to plan when Val is involved which is probably why this book was so entertaining. I wouldn't necessarily say it was a page turner from start to finish - because I did get bored while reading this. <br /><br />Speaking of the people she meets, Lolli, man, she was so freaking weird! That whole killing a cat just because she didn't want to take care of it .. man, it gave me the shivers. I cringed so hard. I don't even like cats that much and I would never do that. AND I'M ALLERGIC TO THEM BITCHES! Besides that, things happened in this book that kind of shocked me a little bit. <br /><br />Overall, it was an interesting book that I'm kind of happy that I dove into. I'm super happy that I dove back into this series and I can't wait to dive into the next book of this one. I hope it's not as creepy or cringe-worthy as this one.. but I'll still probably read it. </span>

<div id="review_6074960" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/6074960" />
    <a title="Lisa Litberg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/264999-lisa-litberg"><img alt="Lisa Litberg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442980399p2/264999.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/6074960?book_show_action=true">Sep 11, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Litberg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Litberg" href="/user/show/264999-lisa-litberg">Lisa Litberg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer6074960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer812073872199459539">I have mixed feelings about this book. I found the idea of the story captivating. Faeries are real, and they walk among us, hidden by glamour from human eyes. And they aren't necessarily good faeries--like humans, some are good, and some are stealthy. 17 year old Val discovers this world when she runs away from home and lives under the New York subway tunnels. Through unforeseen circumstances, she ends up indebted to a troll, delivering potions to faeries. But faeries are being poisoned, and Val</span>
  <span id="freeText812073872199459539" style="display:none">I have mixed feelings about this book. I found the idea of the story captivating. Faeries are real, and they walk among us, hidden by glamour from human eyes. And they aren't necessarily good faeries--like humans, some are good, and some are stealthy. 17 year old Val discovers this world when she runs away from home and lives under the New York subway tunnels. Through unforeseen circumstances, she ends up indebted to a troll, delivering potions to faeries. But faeries are being poisoned, and Val ends up risking her life to solve the mystery and protect her unlikely troll-friend. <br /><br />I liked the premise. And I found myself drawn into the love story that unfolded between Val and Ravus, the troll. Unfortunately, I thought the writing was inconsistent. The plot seemed choppy and the characters were underdeveloped. The story didn't "flow" well enough from one scene to the next, making it less believeable. There were a lot of loose ends at the close of the story which seemed to have been forgotten, or pushed aside, and which I would have liked to seen closed. <br /><br />But even though I was disappointed by this book in many ways, the lure of the faerie world stays with me. I might try reading something else by her, just for more of that...</span>
  <a data-text-id="812073872199459539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_24874697" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=read-in-my-teens">read-in-my-teens</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=age-ya">age-ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=f-audiobook">f-audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=cr-faerie">cr-faerie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1250419-miss-bookiverse?shelf=ge-paranormal">ge-paranormal</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
                  <em>
                    This review has been hidden because it contains spoilers. To view it,
                    <a href="#" onclick="Effect.toggle(&#39;reviewTextContainer24874697&#39;); return false;">click here.</a>
                  </em>
              <span id="reviewTextContainer24874697" class="readable"
                    style="display:none"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16895280361843510468">What finally made me listen to this audiobook I've had for months was a Twilight secret in which someone claimed that Ravus was so much better/hotter than Edward Cullen even though he was a troll. That made me very curious so I gave it a listen. It only took me a few days to finish it. Renee Raudman reads the book in a wonderful, calm way. She does the different voices perfectly, especially Ravus'.<br/><br/>I remember that I had stumbled across Holly Black's website some years ago and thought of her as so</span>
  <span id="freeText16895280361843510468" style="display:none">What finally made me listen to this audiobook I've had for months was a Twilight secret in which someone claimed that Ravus was so much better/hotter than Edward Cullen even though he was a troll. That made me very curious so I gave it a listen. It only took me a few days to finish it. Renee Raudman reads the book in a wonderful, calm way. She does the different voices perfectly, especially Ravus'.<br /><br />I remember that I had stumbled across Holly Black's website some years ago and thought of her as some "wannabe writer", I take that back now. She's a fantastic writer. Her imagination is great, her characters are modern and have depth and she uses language very well. Her style is quite fast and if you don't pay attention for a minute you might lose track but I prefer that to books with tons of unnecessary, boring paragraphs.<br />Furthermore I find her style very real and honest, she doesn't mind describing disgusting/disturbing things (not in a sensational way though, just very casual), for example how Lolli pushes the kitten in front of the train or how Dave and Val have sex.<br /><br />What I loved as well was the anti-heroness about Val. How she shaves off her hair, gets dirtier every day and still is loved. And all the stuff about the Never, the drug similarities, such an interesting idea!<br /><br />The only thing that put me off a little was the beginning when Val discovers the affair between her mom and her boyfriend. I know this is an important event to get the story started and I supposed it has happened before but it just seemed so unrealistic and weird (yes, I know, "unrealistic" might be the wrong word in a fantasy novel).<br /><br />Another thing I loved was the ending. Lots of books I've enjoyed during reading them, have disappointed me with their weak endings. Valiant's last sentence was exactly right and perfectly fitting.<br /><br />All in all a fabulous book about a modern fairytale.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16895280361843510468" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_20880624" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/20880624" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1019098-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451676598p2/1019098.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/20880624?book_show_action=true">Apr 24, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1019098-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">posers, wanna-bes and those looking to flush their lives away</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer20880624" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17401122211848477037">I hated this book from the first page. <br/><br/>Strong words, I know, but let's just have it out. <br/><br/>Trite, lame and basically a waste of tree. The plot was blurg, the characters were frighteningly unenthralling, the writing was fair, but you can find decent writing on the back of a cereal box. <br/><br/>The one book's one saving grace was a troll and though the idea was cool, it was hardly enough to save the entire horrible mess. <br/><br/>To rant in depth, I have to start with the drug thing. Magic as a drug (seen it! and it</span>
  <span id="freeText17401122211848477037" style="display:none">I hated this book from the first page. <br /><br />Strong words, I know, but let's just have it out. <br /><br />Trite, lame and basically a waste of tree. The plot was blurg, the characters were frighteningly unenthralling, the writing was fair, but you can find decent writing on the back of a cereal box. <br /><br />The one book's one saving grace was a troll and though the idea was cool, it was hardly enough to save the entire horrible mess. <br /><br />To rant in depth, I have to start with the drug thing. Magic as a drug (seen it! and it was done better) is an interesting idea, but to depict it as being like heroin addiction seems to be pushing the line just to push the line. <br /><br />And that's the big problem I have with Black. Her characters, her plot, they're constructed like cheap, ugly whores. They have to wear a hellva lot of horrid make-up and will do just about anything to make a few bucks in order to pay their pimps. From the very beginning she's throwing in Jerry Springer-esque turns in what begins to feel like a tacky attempt to hook through shock. <br /><br />Okay, so street kids and drugs and people with piercings and dyed hair, yeah, I know how those things look cool. And being someone who has experience with all of the above, I can't say that I don't appreciate them. But underlying all of these "cool" things is generally such pain and insecurity that to write about them in the way that Black does is like covering a snake-infested swamp with a glittery plastic sheet and inviting your friends to go ice skating.<br /><br />People can write whatever crap they want, thankfully we don't have to read it. <br /><br /> </span>
  <a data-text-id="17401122211848477037" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3509015341" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3509015341" />
    <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads"><img alt="Amy Imogene Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548082309p2/84702001.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3509015341?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amy Imogene Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amy Imogene Reads" href="/user/show/84702001-amy-imogene-reads">Amy Imogene Reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/84702001-amy-imogene-reads?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3509015341" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7650293079361384414">3 stars<br/><br/>For my thoughts on book one, <i>Tithe</i>, see <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629010335' rel='nofollow noopener'>this review.</a> My reviews for this series are reaction reviews, so please check the title page for a description. <br/><br/>This is such an interesting series to me. Not necessarily because of the strength of the plots or storytelling, but because it's an almost near-perfect excavation of a very particular YA trope niche in the mid-2000s. <br/><br/>After <i>Tithe</i>, this was an odd second novel - it follows a completely different set of characters and tackles different themes</span>
  <span id="freeText7650293079361384414" style="display:none">3 stars<br /><br />For my thoughts on book one, <i>Tithe</i>, see <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2629010335" rel="nofollow noopener">this review.</a> My reviews for this series are reaction reviews, so please check the title page for a description. <br /><br />This is such an interesting series to me. Not necessarily because of the strength of the plots or storytelling, but because it's an almost near-perfect excavation of a very particular YA trope niche in the mid-2000s. <br /><br />After <i>Tithe</i>, this was an odd second novel - it follows a completely different set of characters and tackles different themes. In particular, teenage runaways, homelessness, drug use, and faerie politics. To name a few. <br /><br />Because of those harder themes and lack of connection to <i>Tithe</i>, I have to admit I didn't enjoy this novel as much as the first one DESPITE it having a stronger plot, better pacing, and more logical scene transitions. (I'm not a fan of reading/watching/witnessing hardcore drug use due to personal reasons, so that was definitely a me thing and not the fault of the book.) <br /><br />However, what brought this novel up to three stars was its stellar ending sequence. The last 15% of this was awesome, and had all of the best elements of urban/speculative faerie fantasies with a dark twist. <br /><br />Really interesting to see Holly Black continue to explore the threads of faerie culture that she hones in later series, and in this book in particular, I also see some similarities in theme and tone to one of her other books, The Coldest Girl in Coldtown. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.amyimogenereads.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/amyimogenereads/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7650293079361384414" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_37131900" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/37131900" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1690485-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1263584372p2/1690485.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/37131900?book_show_action=true">Nov 07, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/1690485-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">teen fans of fantasy novels</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer37131900" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13122590792364864640">Valiant by Holly Black <br/><br/><br/>Valiant by Holly Black is a very intense teen-fantasy novel about a seventeen-year-old girl named Valerie Russell-also known as: Val. Valiant is Holly Black’s second novel. The first to her collection is Tithe. Both of these books are beautifully written and tie into the world of faeries and trolls and things of such nature. Black is an avid collector of scary stories, creepy dolls, and crazy hats.<br/><br/>Val is this amazing character who changes drastically throughout this book. </span>
  <span id="freeText13122590792364864640" style="display:none">Valiant by Holly Black <br /><br /><br />Valiant by Holly Black is a very intense teen-fantasy novel about a seventeen-year-old girl named Valerie Russell-also known as: Val. Valiant is Holly Black’s second novel. The first to her collection is Tithe. Both of these books are beautifully written and tie into the world of faeries and trolls and things of such nature. Black is an avid collector of scary stories, creepy dolls, and crazy hats.<br /><br />Val is this amazing character who changes drastically throughout this book. By the end, she is a completely different individual. The suspense and action in this book is what kept me thirsting for more and more. There is added humor that makes this reading that much more worth while.<br /><br />A major theme in this novel is that fighting for who you are, what you love and believe in, and what you know is the truth can not only benefit you, but also everybody else, in the end of a torturous situation. Even if it takes all the blood and sweat in Valerie Russell’s body, she is not going down without a fight. Val’s hardworking drive serves as both her strength and weakness in the book.<br /><br />Val’s journey takes place in the suburbs of New York, New York, where she has ran away from home. Heartbroken and devastated from her horrific discovery that her own mother was making out with and cheating on her with her boyfriend, Tom, she boards a train and escapes into the crowded New York streets. While aboard, she cuts her long hair to a buzz, hoping that it will give her some feeling of dignity; she wants a new identity to escape the realness of her situation.<br /><br />Turning off her phone and cutting off all contact with her friends and her family, Val runs into two teens at a local café; Dave and Lolli are two rebellious advocates. Lolli takes Val in under her wing. However, when Dave and Lolli arrive to their so-called home in a subway labyrinth, Luis, Dave’s older brother who is also the ‘leader’, is very displeased but decides to put up with the new intruder anyways.<br /><br />Val notices that things are a little bit creepy around the place but decides to shake it off and just “go with the flow”. One day Val goes along with Dave on one of his deliveries and discovers the mystical world she had only heard of that involves faeries and glamour.<br /><br />After becoming more and more fond of this new-found world, she decides she wants to try and become a part of it and shoots up a magical drug that Lolli and Dave have been using for a while, that they like to call Never; “Nevermore, never, never…no more pain”. No more times that twice a week, and no more times than once a day. This drug allows mortals to have glamour to mask their appearance and make them seem unbelievably beautiful and horrifyingly manipulative. They get everything they ask for and never feel a thing until the drug starts to wear away.<br /><br />While on the Never, Lolli and Val decide to go check out a specific place where Dave makes his deliveries; the home of a troll that goes by the name of Ravus. Ravus was put into exile by the order of the faerie queen because of a sword fight against his best friend, Tamson, which had gone terribly wrong. He is also the maker of Nevermore and while trying to break into his house, they are attacked by a gorgeous glass sword. Short moments after their arrival, the troll shows up and makes an attempt to punish the two girls, however, Val escapes, leaving Lolli. As a trade for Lolli’s freedom Val agrees to do deliveries for Ravus. <br /><br />While on the way to do a delivery, Val witnesses something terrible; there is a dead mermaid lurking above the water; a Folk. Ravus arrives, once again just in time, and informs her of the poisonings that have been happening and that he is a main suspect because of the potions that he makes; the potions she and Dave have been delivering.<br /><br />Val is now severely caught up in a heap of trouble along with Dave, Lolli, Luis, and Ravus. In the midst of trying to escape, Val hears an unbelievably familiar voice; it’s Ruth-her best friends whom she’d been avoiding and ignoring for almost a month. Lolli had agreed to lead her to Val if she’d shut up. Val is frustrated and relieved all at the same time.<br /><br />Now not only is Val caught up in the mystery, but Ruth is too. The entire gang has their lives at stake and who will be to blame? Will Ravus end up being the culprit and will Ruth and Val make it out alive? Are Dave, Lolli, and Luis the ones to blame for the Folk poisonings, or is it the wicked Mabry-who was also put into exile because Ravus killed her love, Tamson? Val’s mother is worried sick and there are many lives to be saved and many mysteries to be unveiled. However, to unmask the unknown, you must read this mythically majestic novel, ever so wonderfully written by the great Holly Black!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Genre: Teen-Fiction/Fantasy<br /><br />Page Count: 320<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="13122590792364864640" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13278290600587269016">Okay, I was so surprised when I picked this one up and found out that it wasn't about Kaye. I honestly didn't even read the synopsis because I wanted to go into it surprised but still, I assumed it would follow the characters from Tithe.<br/><br/>Book two was just as weird as the first one (possible weirder) with a lot of questioning situations to be honest.   <span id="freeText13278290600587269016" style="display:none">Okay, I was so surprised when I picked this one up and found out that it wasn't about Kaye. I honestly didn't even read the synopsis because I wanted to go into it surprised but still, I assumed it would follow the characters from Tithe.<br /><br />Book two was just as weird as the first one (possible weirder) with a lot of questioning situations to be honest. In this one we follow Val and all the strange events that she goes through. Another girl who meets the Faerie realm and its inhabitants. Ravus was also a complete sweetheart! I mean I never thought I'd say this about a troll but it is what it is. This whole book was a whirlwind of the strangest kind and even though I read it in one sitting I didn't love it as much as I did the first one. The characters were at a level of annoying. The only really liked Val (even though she did make some really dumb choices at times) and of course Ravus because he was different.</span>

Blech. She finds refuge with a group of teenage squatters: <b>Lolli, Dave, and Luis</b>. They give her the nickname <i>Prince Valiant</i> and later disclose to her that they are in regular contact with the troll, <b>Ravus</b>.   <span id="freeText4036987241174083236" style="display:none">In <b>Valiant</b>, we meet <b>Valerie</b>. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1547420409ra/26912512.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Val cuts off her hair and runs away to New York City upon discovering that her mother and her boyfriend, Tom, were <i>having an affair</i>. Blech. She finds refuge with a group of teenage squatters: <b>Lolli, Dave, and Luis</b>. They give her the nickname <i>Prince Valiant</i> and later disclose to her that they are in regular contact with the troll, <b>Ravus</b>. He creates <i>Glamour</i>, which exiled faeries use to make their bodies resistant to iron. Glamour is also used by mortals as the addictive drug, <i>Nevermore</i>. Like her friends, Val, gets addicted to it because <b>mortals can do magic</b> for a short time, under the influence of it. Their lives take a turn for the worse, however, when the exiles turn up <b>poisoned</b> and Ravus is blamed for a crime that he <i>did not commit</i>. Val and the others need to find the faery responsible in order to clear Ravus’ name. </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219578304" />
    <a title=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/703854-rebecca"><img alt=" ♥ Rebecca ♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529467844p2/703854.jpg" /></a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=faeries">faeries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=own-physical-copy">own-physical-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/703854-rebecca?shelf=to-reread">to-reread</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer219578304" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16584504524845604624">I thought Kaye, the main character of the first book, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_' title='Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Tithe</a>, had a difficult childhood, but it was nothing compared to this. I wonder if <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black' title='Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>Holly Black</a> had a difficult childhood too. <br/><br/>Most of the book follows Val and her friends Lolli, Dave, and Luis who live in a disgusting, abandoned subway station, while they are high on faerie drugs all day. Val even starts acting like Alex DeLarge at one point when she breaks into a family's home. Lolli kills a cat at one point because she is just tired of taki</span>
  <span id="freeText16584504524845604624" style="display:none">I thought Kaye, the main character of the first book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/46777.Tithe__Modern_Faerie_Tales___1_" title="Tithe (Modern Faerie Tales, #1) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Tithe</a>, had a difficult childhood, but it was nothing compared to this. I wonder if <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/25422.Holly_Black" title="Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Holly Black</a> had a difficult childhood too. <br /><br />Most of the book follows Val and her friends Lolli, Dave, and Luis who live in a disgusting, abandoned subway station, while they are high on faerie drugs all day. Val even starts acting like Alex DeLarge at one point when she breaks into a family's home. Lolli kills a cat at one point because she is just tired of taking care of it. There is also cutting and casual sex among friends. So just be warned it might not be for the very young.<br /><br />The best part is Ravus, the troll Val falls in love with. Ravus is extremely sympathetic. It was hard to get an image of him in my mind but I gathered he looked basically human, except with slightly green skin and large teeth. Val's narrative never described him as handsome, but she did say he was tall and lean, with gorgeous yellow eyes and long, silky black hair. I really enjoyed his character, although he was way too good for Val. <br /><br />Roiben was actually in this one for a bit near the end, and Kaye was mentioned to be in the room, but we don't see her. I know the next book, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/283494.Ironside__Modern_Faerie_Tales___3_" title="Ironside (Modern Faerie Tales, #3) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">Ironside</a>, is about Roiben and Kaye again, but I don't know how important the events in Valiant will be to that story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="16584504524845604624" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <a title="Claire" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/139895-claire"><img alt="Claire" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1182389602p2/139895.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2341895?book_show_action=true">Jun 24, 2007</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claire" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claire" href="/user/show/139895-claire">Claire</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

           <span class="uitext reviewText">anyone who likes Charles de Lint</span></div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2341895" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13451659908733544203">I was a bit disappointed when <i>Valiant</i> didn't start up where <i>Tithe</i> ended. However, I quickly got over it. <br/><br/>This story follows 17-year-old Val Russell who runs away from her dysfunctional home within the first few chapters. In a moment of shedding her confusion, she embraces a new identity and shaves her head, leaving everything behind. She also finds herself in the company of three homeless teens--Lolli, Dave, and Luis who live on an abandoned subway platform.<br/><br/>Eerie and strange, Val finds herself c</span>
  <span id="freeText13451659908733544203" style="display:none">I was a bit disappointed when <i>Valiant</i> didn't start up where <i>Tithe</i> ended. However, I quickly got over it. <br /><br />This story follows 17-year-old Val Russell who runs away from her dysfunctional home within the first few chapters. In a moment of shedding her confusion, she embraces a new identity and shaves her head, leaving everything behind. She also finds herself in the company of three homeless teens--Lolli, Dave, and Luis who live on an abandoned subway platform.<br /><br />Eerie and strange, Val finds herself caught in the web of drugs she's never seen, and a life she never imagined. Luis is severe, blind in one eye, and pierced with iron. He also wears the role of protector for both Lolli and Dave. He's none too happy to find Val among them. <br /><br />Dave is the younger brother who mistakenly takes Val on a delivery her first morning with the trio. With him, she finds the web of glamour that will keep her from ever seeing anything the same way again.<br /><br />Under the blanket of the world of faerie, she finds someone to stand up for and takes control of her future. I can't wait for <i>Ironside</i> which picks up Roiben and Kaye's continuing story.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13451659908733544203" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2882445499" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15619018840540272665">This story was much too disconcerting for me to thoroughly enjoy. To be frank, I think that I liked it better when Holly Black's Faerie stories were centred on the Seelie and Unseelie Courts. There was much more intrigue, and a sense of newness and discovering something unknown.<br/><br/>The stories that are based in OUR world, aren't as strong. And the protagonists... are a bit more from the seedier side of life.<br/><br/>This was true here. Val comes from a home of a single mum, and upon discovering a secret - in</span>
  <span id="freeText15619018840540272665" style="display:none">This story was much too disconcerting for me to thoroughly enjoy. To be frank, I think that I liked it better when Holly Black's Faerie stories were centred on the Seelie and Unseelie Courts. There was much more intrigue, and a sense of newness and discovering something unknown.<br /><br />The stories that are based in OUR world, aren't as strong. And the protagonists... are a bit more from the seedier side of life.<br /><br />This was true here. Val comes from a home of a single mum, and upon discovering a secret - instead of confronting the people involved - she runs away. What follows is some pretty graphic depictions of drug use, messed up morals of people (and Fae) trying to simply survive, and pretty out-of-left field declarations of love.<br /><br />The writing was solid, as it always is. The reveal was pretty good, but it just wasn't my cup of tea.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15619018840540272665" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2407582196" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2407582196" />
    <a title="Sophie Elaina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/54237690-sophie-elaina"><img alt="Sophie Elaina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572297086p2/54237690.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2407582196?book_show_action=true">Nov 19, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sophie Elaina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sophie Elaina" href="/user/show/54237690-sophie-elaina">Sophie Elaina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9781534484535" href="/book/show/52730667-valiant">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=read-in-2019">read-in-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-paperbacks">owned-paperbacks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-read">owned-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=2-star">2-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=owned-hardcovers">owned-hardcovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/54237690-sophie-elaina?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2407582196" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17655849802609480601">I have a lot of emotions about this book. I found that I either loved what was happening or hated what was happening. Nothing was middle ground and I feel kind of odd giving it a three star rating because of it. I loved the dark nitty grittiness of the story and the main character Val; but at the same time I think a lot of things that were being focused on would’ve worked better if they were more like underlying themes and less at the forefront of the book. I needed more faeries and magic, don’t</span>
  <span id="freeText17655849802609480601" style="display:none">I have a lot of emotions about this book. I found that I either loved what was happening or hated what was happening. Nothing was middle ground and I feel kind of odd giving it a three star rating because of it. I loved the dark nitty grittiness of the story and the main character Val; but at the same time I think a lot of things that were being focused on would’ve worked better if they were more like underlying themes and less at the forefront of the book. I needed more faeries and magic, don’t get me wrong it was there but I feel as though the plot could’ve delved deeper. <br /><br />There is also a scene with a kitten that disappointed me and gave me the worst kind of feeling, so beware going in if you are sensitive to animal deaths and abuse like I am. I feel as though it was a shock factor type of move and it didn’t need to happen. (If you have the new bind up, it’s on page 409. I wish I had known the page number so I could skip it so I’ll leave it here just in case.)<br /><br />While reading this I also listened to the audiobook alongside and noticed quite a few things were changed in the newly published bind up of The Modern Faerie Tales. In a lot of cases this was definitely necessary because there is quite a lot of slang and phrases used towards the beginning of the book that are definitely outdated and can be found offensive, but in the new edition this was corrected. However some hints and tidbits were added to tie in with the Folk of The Air series that weren’t there originally. I’m not sure if it’s just me but this kind of felt like a cheat. There are characters that cross over anyway and work to link the two series so why feel the need to name drop other things too? I see how this could enhance the story if you’ve read the other series then gone back to read this one. But knowing it wasn’t a part of the story originally is weird. <br /><br />As a whole I did find this book more entertaining and just more gripping overall than Tithe. But I’m confused as to my feelings. But I can say that I loved the magic and dark places the story delves into. Holly Black’s writing is intoxicatingly addictive, so even though I didn’t love everything about this I can still say that Black is a favourite of mine and I love the way she writes.<br /><br />Rating: ⭐️⭐️⭐️<br />Full review:<a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.sophieinbookland.com/post/valiant">https://www.sophieinbookland.com/post...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17655849802609480601" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_2925034805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2925034805" />
    <a title="Liliana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71115989-liliana"><img alt="Liliana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504631791p2/71115989.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2925034805?book_show_action=true">Aug 06, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liliana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liliana" href="/user/show/71115989-liliana">Liliana</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71115989-liliana?shelf=sff">sff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2925034805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15590380382569338182">Making my way through Holly Black's Modern Faerie Tales Series and TFOTA before the release of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032912.The_Queen_of_Nothing__The_Folk_of_the_Air___3_' title='The Queen of Nothing (The Folk of the Air, #3) by Holly Black' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Queen of Nothing</a> in November (yes, this year!). Read this after Tithe in what appears to be the right order, and I am equally torn about what rating to give it! Let me try to digest my thoughts.<br/><br/>While set in the same universe as Tithe, Valiant follows different characters, though there are some cameos. As its predecessor, it is characterised as an urban fantasy, succeeding in embedding the reader in</span>
  <span id="freeText15590380382569338182" style="display:none">Making my way through Holly Black's Modern Faerie Tales Series and TFOTA before the release of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26032912.The_Queen_of_Nothing__The_Folk_of_the_Air___3_" title="The Queen of Nothing (The Folk of the Air, #3) by Holly Black" rel="nofollow noopener">The Queen of Nothing</a> in November (yes, this year!). Read this after Tithe in what appears to be the right order, and I am equally torn about what rating to give it! Let me try to digest my thoughts.<br /><br />While set in the same universe as Tithe, Valiant follows different characters, though there are some cameos. As its predecessor, it is characterised as an urban fantasy, succeeding in embedding the reader in this grimy world that has poisoned everyone in some way, whether physically or emotionally, whether human or fae. I love this about Holly Black's writing, how she is able to make the world come alive, and each character have its own voice and 'je ne sais quoi', let's say. Valiant is set more in an urban setting than Tithe, as most of the story is set in the actual streets of New York city, where Val, our MC, is trying to survive with a random group of teens after running away from home. So, not only is she thrust into a huge city full of very human danger, but she has to deal with the newfound knowledge of faeries, and how their magical existence affects her life. We thus deal with very 'fantastical' but also real world problems, as Val lives on the street and squats in the underground subway tunnels, is confronted with drug addiction (***heavy trigger warnings***) and tries to find her place in a world that now seems so foreign and yet so easy, welcoming and hidden.<br /><br />This story is definitely the 'heaviest' and most stressful of the Modern Faerie Tales. It was painful to read at times because of the themes presented. I wanted to reach out and slap Val and tell her to get a grip so many times. It was nonetheless a very compelling story because, or in spite of that. It was very interesting to know about the exiled fae in NYC, and Ravus' character is a precious baby that I want to treasure forever. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ I honestly don't know what he saw in Val "^^  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />The world gets a big expansion with this novel. We learn a lot more about Nevermore (though until I read TFOTA again, I will feel it was a bit retconned), and the effects that it has on humans and fae alike.<br /><br />Overall, characters and world-building made this very enjoyable for me. Plot-wise, I thought it wasn't very well paced, and it dragged at parts. I don't think we needed to dwell on nevermore quite so much and would've liked a lot more on the ending, which felt a little bit rushed. Besides that, while I could relate to Val a lot in the beginning and the end, in the middle of the book her character goes through this idiotic phase that I just couldn't bring myself to like. Holly really likes her MCs to make the dumbest decisions ever. Because of the stressful experience of reading this book due to the themes, and a lack of overall enjoyment due to the uneven pacing, I can't bring myself to give this more than 3*, though I was very invested and enjoyed it quite a bit! I will never tire of this Holly Black universe, I think.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15590380382569338182" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_16794903" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/16794903" />
    <a title="JM" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/687074-jm"><img alt="JM" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1484457729p2/687074.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/16794903?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JM" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JM" href="/user/show/687074-jm">JM</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to JM by: </span>
      Sarah Rees Brennan
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=setting-usa">setting-usa</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=fairytale-elements">fairytale-elements</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=setting-hidden-world">setting-hidden-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/687074-jm?shelf=ya-specfic">ya-specfic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer16794903" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer721806841207256675">YA urban fantasy, loosely based on the story of 'Beauty and the Beast'. Val doesn't entirely mean to run away from home, but when home betrays her it's easy to not go back <i>yet</i> - to stay in the dark world of faeries and addiction she's stumbled into in New York. She's drawn further into that world when a moment of instinctive chivalry sees her bound in service to the troll Ravus - who, Val discovers, is in grave danger.<br/><br/>My short reaction here is: This was a good book, and I didn't like it much.<br/><br/>Lon</span>
  <span id="freeText721806841207256675" style="display:none">YA urban fantasy, loosely based on the story of 'Beauty and the Beast'. Val doesn't entirely mean to run away from home, but when home betrays her it's easy to not go back <i>yet</i> - to stay in the dark world of faeries and addiction she's stumbled into in New York. She's drawn further into that world when a moment of instinctive chivalry sees her bound in service to the troll Ravus - who, Val discovers, is in grave danger.<br /><br />My short reaction here is: This was a good book, and I didn't like it much.<br /><br />Longer reaction: It was good in that Val is a powerful force in the narrative, and she's indisputably the hero of her story; she has a sword to prove it. She's prickly and kick-arse in a completely believable way. She falls in love with a monster, and doesn't need him to be a prince in disguise. And the drug sequences were rather well done - the way that the faery dust makes you powerful, makes your world malleable, is a nice twist. I'm a fan of fairy tale novels, too, and I liked the way that this one incorporated parental betrayal as the impetus for the heroine leaving home, in a different way to the source tale's. Also, this book uses chapter quotations in a way that really works, because they match the tone of the book. (Plus, without them, I might not have noticed the 'Goblin Market' connection, and that would have been sad.)<br /><br />But it didn't grab me. I admired Val, with all her wrong choices, but I didn't especially feel for her. Maybe my subconscious decided that as capable as she was, she could look out for herself - she didn't need me in her corner. Addiction, too, doesn't make you a nice person, and Black shows that; that helps make it real, maybe, but it doesn't make the characters sympathetic. <br /><br />The other principal characters - the two brothers and Lolly - while they were distinctive and well drawn, didn't get much resolution. They started out as the major focus, but then they had to fight with the Val-Ravus story for narrative relevance, and they lost. I didn't want them to. I wanted the brothers, with their rich, tragic backstory, to get something good out of all this, not to end up simply as players in Val and Ravus' story. I wanted Lolly, with no backstory at all, to <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[go somewhere, be ultimately saved somehow - after all, her being saved from a specific danger was the pivot for one of the key sequences of the book. Having her wander off to be lost and messed up somewhere else in the end wasn't much with the satisfying. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Also, the key plot revelation bordered on really obvious, which is always disappointing.<br /><br />Mostly, it just wasn't my style. Angsty heroines and lost boys and people betraying each other apparently aren't my thing, no matter how many faeries you add.</span>
  <a data-text-id="721806841207256675" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
